 </li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><b>Associate members</b>: 
 </li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/23px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/35px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/45px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>

 </li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>
</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Official languages </div></th><td>
<a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Council President</div></th><td>
Sijbrand de Jong<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;"><a href="/wiki/List_of_Directors_General_of_CERN" title="List of Directors General of CERN">Director General</a></div></th><td>
<a href="/wiki/Fabiola_Gianotti" title="Fabiola Gianotti">Fabiola Gianotti</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;">Website</th><td>
<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://home.cern/">home<wbr />.cern</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>European Organization for Nuclear Research</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Organisation européenne pour la recherche nucléaire</i>), known as <b>CERN</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ɜːr/: &#39;ur&#39; in &#39;fur&#39;">ɜːr</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>French pronunciation:&#160;&#8203;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[sɛʁn]</a></span>; derived from the name <i>Conseil européen pour la recherche nucléaire</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> research organization that operates the largest <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">particle physics</a> laboratory in the world. Established in 1954, the organization is based in a northwest suburb of <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a> on the Franco–Swiss border, (<span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=CERN&amp;params=46_14_3_N_6_3_19_E_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">46°14′3″N</span> <span class="longitude">6°3′19″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">46.23417°N 6.05528°E</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">46.23417; 6.05528</span></span></span></a></span>) and has 22 <a href="#Member_states_and_budget">member states</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> is the only non-European country granted full membership.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> CERN is an official <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">United Nations Observer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The acronym CERN is also used to refer to the laboratory, which in 2016 had 2,500 scientific, technical, and administrative staff members, and hosted about 12,000 users. In the same year, CERN generated 49 <a href="/wiki/Petabyte" title="Petabyte">petabytes</a> of data.<sup id="cite_ref-infigures_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infigures-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>CERN's main function is to provide the <a href="/wiki/Particle_accelerator" title="Particle accelerator">particle accelerators</a> and other infrastructure needed for high-energy physics research – as a result, numerous experiments have been constructed at CERN through international collaborations. The main site at <a href="/wiki/Meyrin" title="Meyrin">Meyrin</a> hosts a large computing facility, which is primarily used to <a href="/wiki/Computer_data_storage" title="Computer data storage">store</a> and <a href="/wiki/Data_analysis" title="Data analysis">analyse data</a> from experiments, as well as <a href="/wiki/Simulation" title="Simulation">simulate</a> <a href="/wiki/Event_(particle_physics)" title="Event (particle physics)">events</a>. Researchers need remote access to these facilities, so the lab has historically been a major <a href="/wiki/Wide_area_network" title="Wide area network">wide area network</a> hub. CERN is also the birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AHT_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AHT-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cernfounders.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Cernfounders.png/210px-Cernfounders.png" width="210" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Cernfounders.png/315px-Cernfounders.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Cernfounders.png/420px-Cernfounders.png 2x" data-file-width="1236" data-file-height="1245" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cernfounders.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 12 founding member states of CERN in 1954<sup id="cite_ref-foundation_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundation-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> (map borders from 1954–1990)</div></div></div>
<p>The convention establishing CERN was ratified on 29&#160;September 1954 by 12 countries in Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-foundation_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundation-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The acronym CERN originally represented the French words for <i>Conseil Européen pour la Recherche Nucléaire</i> (European Council for Nuclear Research), which was a provisional council for building the laboratory, established by 12 European governments in 1952. The acronym was retained for the new laboratory after the provisional council was dissolved, even though the name changed to the current <i>Organisation Européenne pour la Recherche Nucléaire</i> (European Organization for Nuclear Research) in 1954.<sup id="cite_ref-cern-name_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cern-name-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Lew_Kowarski" title="Lew Kowarski">Lew Kowarski</a>, a former director of CERN, when the name was changed, the abbreviation could have become the awkward OERN, and <a href="/wiki/Werner_Heisenberg" title="Werner Heisenberg">Heisenberg</a> said that this could "still be CERN even if the name is [not]".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>CERN's first president was Sir <a href="/wiki/Ben_Lockspeiser" title="Ben Lockspeiser">Benjamin Lockspeiser</a>. <a href="/wiki/Edoardo_Amaldi" title="Edoardo Amaldi">Edoardo Amaldi</a> was the general secretary of CERN at its early stages when operations were still provisional, while the first Director-General (1954) was <a href="/wiki/Felix_Bloch" title="Felix Bloch">Felix Bloch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The laboratory was originally devoted to the study of <a href="/wiki/Atomic_nucleus" title="Atomic nucleus">atomic nuclei</a>, but was soon applied to <a href="/wiki/High-energy_physics" class="mw-redirect" title="High-energy physics">higher-energy physics</a>, concerned mainly with the study of interactions between <a href="/wiki/Subatomic_particle" title="Subatomic particle">subatomic particles</a>. Therefore, the laboratory operated by CERN is commonly referred to as the <b>European laboratory for particle physics</b> (<i>Laboratoire européen pour la physique des particules</i>), which better describes the research being performed there.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding_members">Founding members</span></h3>
<p>At the sixth session of the CERN Council, which took place in Paris from 29 June - 1 July 1953, the convention establishing the organization was signed, subject to ratification, by 12 states.
The convention was gradually ratified by the 12 founding Member States: <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, the <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">Federal Republic of Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and <a href="/wiki/SFR_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="SFR Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_achievements">Scientific achievements</span></h3>
<p>Several important achievements in particle physics have been made through experiments at CERN. They include:
</p>
<ul><li>1973: The discovery of <a href="/wiki/Neutral_current" title="Neutral current">neutral currents</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Gargamelle" title="Gargamelle">Gargamelle</a> bubble chamber;<sup id="cite_ref-gargamelle_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gargamelle-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1983: The discovery of <a href="/wiki/W_and_Z_bosons" title="W and Z bosons">W and Z bosons</a> in the <a href="/wiki/UA1_experiment" title="UA1 experiment">UA1</a> and <a href="/wiki/UA2_experiment" title="UA2 experiment">UA2 experiments</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-wz_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wz-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1989: The determination of the number of light <a href="/wiki/Neutrino" title="Neutrino">neutrino</a> families at the <a href="/wiki/Large_Electron%E2%80%93Positron_Collider" title="Large Electron–Positron Collider">Large Electron–Positron Collider</a> (LEP) operating on the Z boson peak;</li>
<li>1995: The first creation of <a href="/wiki/Antihydrogen" title="Antihydrogen">antihydrogen</a> atoms in the <a href="/wiki/PS210_experiment" title="PS210 experiment">PS210 experiment</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-antihydrogen_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-antihydrogen-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1999: The discovery of direct <a href="/wiki/CP_violation" title="CP violation">CP violation</a> in the <a href="/wiki/NA48_experiment" title="NA48 experiment">NA48 experiment</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-NA48_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NA48-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2010: The isolation of 38 atoms of <a href="/wiki/Antihydrogen" title="Antihydrogen">antihydrogen</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Antihydrogen_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Antihydrogen-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2011: Maintaining <a href="/wiki/Antihydrogen" title="Antihydrogen">antihydrogen</a> for over 15 minutes;<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2012: A <a href="/wiki/Boson" title="Boson">boson</a> with mass around 125 GeV/c<sup>2</sup> consistent with the long-sought <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">Higgs boson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>In September 2011, CERN attracted media attention when the <a href="/wiki/OPERA_experiment" title="OPERA experiment">OPERA Collaboration</a> reported the detection of possibly <a href="/wiki/Faster-than-light_neutrino_anomaly" title="Faster-than-light neutrino anomaly">faster-than-light neutrinos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Further tests showed that the results were flawed due to an incorrectly connected <a href="/wiki/GPS" class="mw-redirect" title="GPS">GPS</a> synchronization cable.<sup id="cite_ref-OPERAanomaly_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OPERAanomaly-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1984 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_Physics" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize for Physics">Nobel Prize for Physics</a> was awarded to <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Rubbia" title="Carlo Rubbia">Carlo Rubbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simon_van_der_Meer" title="Simon van der Meer">Simon van der Meer</a> for the developments that resulted in the discoveries of the W and Z bosons. The 1992 Nobel Prize for Physics was awarded to CERN staff researcher <a href="/wiki/Georges_Charpak" title="Georges Charpak">Georges Charpak</a> "for his invention and development of particle detectors, in particular the <a href="/wiki/Multiwire_proportional_chamber" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiwire proportional chamber">multiwire proportional chamber</a>". The 2013 Nobel Prize for physics was awarded to <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Englert" title="François Englert">François Englert</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Higgs" title="Peter Higgs">Peter Higgs</a> for the theoretical description of the Higgs mechanism in the year after the Higgs boson was found by CERN experiments.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Computer_science">Computer science</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_World_Wide_Web" title="History of the World Wide Web">History of the World Wide Web</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:715px;max-width:715px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Web_Server.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/First_Web_Server.jpg/250px-First_Web_Server.jpg" width="250" height="188" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/First_Web_Server.jpg/375px-First_Web_Server.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/First_Web_Server.jpg/500px-First_Web_Server.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">This <a href="/wiki/NeXT_Computer" title="NeXT Computer">NeXT Computer</a> used by British scientist <a href="/wiki/Sir_Tim_Berners-Lee" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Tim Berners-Lee">Sir Tim Berners-Lee</a> at CERN became the first <a href="/wiki/Web_server" title="Web server">Web server</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:205px;max-width:205px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciscosystemsrouteratcern.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ciscosystemsrouteratcern.jpg/203px-Ciscosystemsrouteratcern.jpg" width="203" height="189" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ciscosystemsrouteratcern.jpg/305px-Ciscosystemsrouteratcern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ciscosystemsrouteratcern.jpg/406px-Ciscosystemsrouteratcern.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="698" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">This <a href="/wiki/Cisco_Systems" title="Cisco Systems">Cisco Systems</a> router at CERN was one of the first <a href="/wiki/IP_router" class="mw-redirect" title="IP router">IP routers</a> deployed in Europe.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Where_the_WEB_was_born.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Where_the_WEB_was_born.jpg/250px-Where_the_WEB_was_born.jpg" width="250" height="188" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Where_the_WEB_was_born.jpg/375px-Where_the_WEB_was_born.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Where_the_WEB_was_born.jpg/500px-Where_the_WEB_was_born.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A plaque at CERN commemorating the invention of the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a> by <a href="/wiki/Tim_Berners-Lee" title="Tim Berners-Lee">Tim Berners-Lee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Cailliau" title="Robert Cailliau">Robert Cailliau</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a> began as a CERN project named <a href="/wiki/ENQUIRE" title="ENQUIRE">ENQUIRE</a>, initiated by <a href="/wiki/Tim_Berners-Lee" title="Tim Berners-Lee">Tim Berners-Lee</a> in 1989 and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Cailliau" title="Robert Cailliau">Robert Cailliau</a> in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Berners-Lee and Cailliau were jointly honoured by the <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Computing_Machinery" title="Association for Computing Machinery">Association for Computing Machinery</a> in 1995 for their contributions to the development of the World Wide Web.
</p><p>Based on the concept of <a href="/wiki/Hypertext" title="Hypertext">hypertext</a>, the project was intended to facilitate the sharing of information between researchers. The first website was activated in 1991. On 30&#160;April 1993, CERN announced that the World Wide Web would be free to anyone. A copy<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.w3.org/History/19921103-hypertext/hypertext/WWW/TheProject.html">the original first webpage</a>, created by Berners-Lee, is still published on the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web_Consortium" title="World Wide Web Consortium">World Wide Web Consortium</a>'s website as a historical document.
</p><p>Prior to the Web's development, CERN had pioneered the introduction of Internet technology, beginning in the early 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>More recently, CERN has become a facility for the development of <a href="/wiki/Grid_computing" title="Grid computing">grid computing</a>, hosting projects including the <a href="/wiki/Enabling_Grids_for_E-sciencE" class="mw-redirect" title="Enabling Grids for E-sciencE">Enabling Grids for E-sciencE</a> (EGEE) and <a href="/wiki/LHC_Computing_Grid" class="mw-redirect" title="LHC Computing Grid">LHC Computing Grid</a>. It also hosts the <a href="/wiki/CERN_Internet_Exchange_Point" title="CERN Internet Exchange Point">CERN Internet Exchange Point</a> (CIXP), one of the two main <a href="/wiki/Internet_exchange_point" title="Internet exchange point">internet exchange points</a> in Switzerland.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Particle_accelerators">Particle accelerators</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_complex">Current complex</span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><caption><a class="mw-selflink selflink">CERN</a> <a href="/wiki/Particle_accelerator" title="Particle accelerator">accelerator complex</a></caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<a href="/wiki/File:Cern-accelerator-complex.svg" class="image"><img alt="Cern-accelerator-complex.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Cern-accelerator-complex.svg/250px-Cern-accelerator-complex.svg.png" width="250" height="163" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Cern-accelerator-complex.svg/375px-Cern-accelerator-complex.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Cern-accelerator-complex.svg/500px-Cern-accelerator-complex.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1394" data-file-height="908" /></a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">List of current particle <br /> accelerators at CERN</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/CERN_Hadron_LINACs#LINAC_2" class="mw-redirect" title="CERN Hadron LINACs">Linac 2</a></th><td>
Accelerates <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">protons</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/CERN_Hadron_LINACs#LINAC_3" class="mw-redirect" title="CERN Hadron LINACs">Linac 3</a></th><td>
Accelerates <a href="/wiki/Ions" class="mw-redirect" title="Ions">ions</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/CERN_Hadron_LINACs#LINAC_4" class="mw-redirect" title="CERN Hadron LINACs">Linac 4</a></th><td>
Accelerates negative <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_ions" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrogen ions">hydrogen ions</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Antiproton_Decelerator" title="Antiproton Decelerator">AD</a></th><td>
Decelerates <a href="/wiki/Antiprotons" class="mw-redirect" title="Antiprotons">antiprotons</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">LHC</a></th><td>
Collides protons or heavy <a href="/wiki/Ions" class="mw-redirect" title="Ions">ions</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Low_Energy_Ion_Ring" title="Low Energy Ion Ring">LEIR</a></th><td>
Accelerates <a href="/wiki/Ions" class="mw-redirect" title="Ions">ions</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Proton_Synchrotron_Booster" title="Proton Synchrotron Booster">PSB</a></th><td>
Accelerates protons or ions</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Proton_Synchrotron" title="Proton Synchrotron">PS</a></th><td>
Accelerates protons or ions</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Super_Proton_Synchrotron" title="Super Proton Synchrotron">SPS</a></th><td>
Accelerates protons or ions</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Location_Large_Hadron_Collider.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Location_Large_Hadron_Collider.PNG/220px-Location_Large_Hadron_Collider.PNG" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Location_Large_Hadron_Collider.PNG/330px-Location_Large_Hadron_Collider.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Location_Large_Hadron_Collider.PNG/440px-Location_Large_Hadron_Collider.PNG 2x" data-file-width="518" data-file-height="518" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Location_Large_Hadron_Collider.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">Large Hadron Collider</a> together with the <a href="/wiki/Super_Proton_Synchrotron" title="Super Proton Synchrotron">Super Proton Synchrotron</a> at CERN</div></div></div>
<p>CERN operates a network of six accelerators and a decelerator. Each machine in the chain increases the energy of particle beams before delivering them to experiments or to the next more powerful accelerator. Currently active machines are:
</p>
<ul><li>Two <a href="/wiki/Linear_accelerator" class="mw-redirect" title="Linear accelerator">linear accelerators</a> generate low energy particles. <a href="/wiki/LINAC_2" class="mw-redirect" title="LINAC 2">LINAC 2</a> accelerates protons to 50&#160;<a href="/wiki/Megaelectronvolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megaelectronvolt">MeV</a> for injection into the Proton Synchrotron Booster (PSB), and <a href="/wiki/LINAC_3" class="mw-redirect" title="LINAC 3">LINAC 3</a> provides heavy ions at 4.2&#160;MeV/<a href="/wiki/Atomic_mass_unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Atomic mass unit">u</a> for injection into the Low Energy Ion Ring (LEIR).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Proton_Synchrotron_Booster" title="Proton Synchrotron Booster">Proton Synchrotron Booster</a> increases the energy of particles generated by the proton linear accelerator before they are transferred to the other accelerators.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Low_Energy_Ion_Ring" title="Low Energy Ion Ring">Low Energy Ion Ring</a> (LEIR) accelerates the ions from the ion linear accelerator, before transferring them to the <a href="/wiki/Proton_Synchrotron" title="Proton Synchrotron">Proton Synchrotron</a> (PS). This <a href="/wiki/Particle_accelerator" title="Particle accelerator">accelerator</a> was commissioned in 2005, after having been reconfigured from the previous <a href="/wiki/Low_Energy_Antiproton_Ring" title="Low Energy Antiproton Ring">Low Energy Antiproton Ring</a> (LEAR).</li>
<li>The 28 <a href="/wiki/Gigaelectronvolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Gigaelectronvolt">GeV</a> <a href="/wiki/Proton_Synchrotron" title="Proton Synchrotron">Proton Synchrotron</a> (PS), built during 1954—1959 and still operating as a feeder to the more powerful <a href="/wiki/Super_Proton_Synchrotron" title="Super Proton Synchrotron">SPS</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Super_Proton_Synchrotron" title="Super Proton Synchrotron">Super Proton Synchrotron</a> (SPS), a circular accelerator with a diameter of 2 kilometres built in a tunnel, which started operation in 1976. It was designed to deliver an energy of 300&#160;GeV and was gradually upgraded to 450&#160;GeV. As well as having its own beamlines for fixed-target experiments (currently <a href="/wiki/COMPASS_experiment" title="COMPASS experiment">COMPASS</a> and <a href="/wiki/NA62_experiment" title="NA62 experiment">NA62</a>), it has been operated as a <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">proton</a>–<a href="/wiki/Antiproton" title="Antiproton">antiproton</a> <a href="/wiki/Collider" title="Collider">collider</a> (the Sp<span style="text-decoration:overline;">p</span>S collider), and for accelerating high energy <a href="/wiki/Electron" title="Electron">electrons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Positron" title="Positron">positrons</a> which were injected into the <a href="/wiki/Large_Electron%E2%80%93Positron_Collider" title="Large Electron–Positron Collider">Large Electron–Positron Collider</a> (LEP). Since 2008, it has been used to inject protons and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heavy_ion&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Heavy ion (page does not exist)">heavy ions</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">Large Hadron Collider</a> (LHC).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/On-Line_Isotope_Mass_Separator" title="On-Line Isotope Mass Separator">On-Line Isotope Mass Separator</a> (ISOLDE), which is used to study <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_decay" title="Radioactive decay">unstable nuclei</a>. The radioactive ions are produced by the impact of protons at an energy of 1.0–1.4&#160;GeV from the Proton Synchrotron Booster. It was first commissioned in 1967 and was rebuilt with major upgrades in 1974 and 1992.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Antiproton_Decelerator" title="Antiproton Decelerator">Antiproton Decelerator</a> (AD), which reduces the velocity of antiprotons to about 10% of the <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">speed of light</a> for research of <a href="/wiki/Antimatter" title="Antimatter">antimatter</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Compact_Linear_Collider" title="Compact Linear Collider">Compact Linear Collider</a> Test Facility, which studies feasibility for the future normal conducting linear collider project.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/AWAKE" title="AWAKE">AWAKE</a> experiment, which is a proof-of-principle <a href="/wiki/Plasma_acceleration" title="Plasma acceleration">plasma wakefield accelerator</a>.</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Large_Hadron_Collider">Large Hadron Collider</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">Large Hadron Collider</a></div>
<p>Many activities at CERN currently involve operating the <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">Large Hadron Collider</a> (LHC) and the experiments for it. The LHC represents a large-scale, worldwide scientific cooperation project.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Construction_of_LHC_at_CERN.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Construction_of_LHC_at_CERN.jpg/170px-Construction_of_LHC_at_CERN.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Construction_of_LHC_at_CERN.jpg/255px-Construction_of_LHC_at_CERN.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b9/Construction_of_LHC_at_CERN.jpg 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Construction_of_LHC_at_CERN.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Construction of the <a href="/wiki/Compact_Muon_Solenoid" title="Compact Muon Solenoid">CMS</a> detector for <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">LHC</a> at CERN</div></div></div>
<p>The LHC tunnel is located 100 metres underground, in the region between the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Geneva International Airport">Geneva International Airport</a> and the nearby <a href="/wiki/Jura_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Jura mountains">Jura mountains</a>. The majority of its length is on the French side of the border. It uses the 27&#160;km circumference circular tunnel previously occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Large_Electron%E2%80%93Positron_Collider" title="Large Electron–Positron Collider">Large Electron–Positron Collider</a> (LEP), which was shut down in November 2000. CERN's existing PS/SPS accelerator complexes are used to pre-accelerate protons and lead ions which are then injected into the LHC.
</p><p>Seven experiments (<a href="/wiki/Compact_Muon_Solenoid" title="Compact Muon Solenoid">CMS</a>, <a href="/wiki/ATLAS_experiment" title="ATLAS experiment">ATLAS</a>, <a href="/wiki/LHCb" class="mw-redirect" title="LHCb">LHCb</a>, <a href="/wiki/MoEDAL_experiment" title="MoEDAL experiment">MoEDAL</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/TOTEM" class="mw-redirect" title="TOTEM">TOTEM</a>, <a href="/wiki/LHCf" class="mw-redirect" title="LHCf">LHC-forward</a> and <a href="/wiki/A_Large_Ion_Collider_Experiment" class="mw-redirect" title="A Large Ion Collider Experiment">ALICE</a>) are located along the collider; each of them studies particle collisions from a different aspect, and with different technologies. Construction for these experiments required an extraordinary engineering effort. For example, a special <a href="/wiki/Crane_(machine)" title="Crane (machine)">crane</a> was rented from Belgium to lower pieces of the CMS detector into its underground cavern, since each piece weighed nearly 2,000 tons. The first of the approximately 5,000 magnets necessary for construction was lowered down a special shaft at 13:00&#160;<a href="/wiki/GMT" class="mw-redirect" title="GMT">GMT</a> on 7 March 2005.
</p><p>The LHC has begun to generate vast quantities of data, which CERN streams to laboratories around the world for distributed processing (making use of a specialized <a href="/wiki/Grid_computing" title="Grid computing">grid</a> infrastructure, the <a href="/wiki/LHC_Computing_Grid" class="mw-redirect" title="LHC Computing Grid">LHC Computing Grid</a>). During April 2005, a trial successfully streamed 600&#160;MB/s to seven different sites across the world.
</p><p>The initial particle beams were injected into the LHC August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT2008/07/29_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT2008/07/29-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The first beam was circulated through the entire LHC on 10 September 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-CERNPR06.08_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CERNPR06.08-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> but the system failed 10 days later because of a faulty magnet connection, and it was stopped for repairs on 19 September 2008.
</p><p>The LHC resumed operation on 20 November 2009 by successfully circulating two beams, each with an energy of 3.5&#160;tera<a href="/wiki/Electronvolts" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronvolts">electronvolts</a> (TeV). The challenge for the engineers was then to try to line up the two beams so that they smashed into each other. This is like "firing two needles across the Atlantic and getting them to hit each other" according to Steve Myers, director for accelerators and technology.
</p><p>On 30 March 2010, the LHC successfully collided two proton beams with 3.5 TeV of energy per proton, resulting in a 7 TeV collision energy. However, this was just the start of what was needed for the expected discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">Higgs boson</a>. When the 7 TeV experimental period ended, the LHC revved to 8 TeV (4 TeV per proton) starting March 2012, and soon began particle collisions at that energy. In July 2012, CERN scientists announced the discovery of a new sub-atomic particle that was later confirmed to be the <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">Higgs boson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
In March 2013, CERN announced that the measurements performed on the newly found particle allowed it to conclude that this is a Higgs boson.<sup id="cite_ref-intersitetunnel_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-intersitetunnel-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In early 2013, the LHC was deactivated for a two-year maintenance period, to strengthen the electrical connections between magnets inside the accelerator and for other upgrades.
</p><p>On 5 April 2015, after two years of maintenance and consolidation, the LHC restarted for a second run. The first ramp to the record-breaking energy of 6.5 TeV was performed on 10 April 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the design collision rate was exceeded for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> A second two-year period of shutdown is scheduled to begin at the end of 2018.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Decommissioned_accelerators">Decommissioned accelerators</span></h3>
<ul><li>The original linear accelerator (<a href="/wiki/LINAC_1" class="mw-redirect" title="LINAC 1">LINAC 1</a>).</li>
<li>The 600&#160;MeV <a href="/wiki/Synchrocyclotron" title="Synchrocyclotron">Synchrocyclotron</a> (SC) which started operation in 1957 and was shut down in 1991.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Intersecting_Storage_Rings" title="Intersecting Storage Rings">Intersecting Storage Rings</a> (ISR), an early collider built from 1966 to 1971 and operated until 1984.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Large_Electron%E2%80%93Positron_Collider" title="Large Electron–Positron Collider">Large Electron–Positron Collider</a> (LEP), which operated from 1989 to 2000 and was the largest machine of its kind, housed in a 27&#160;km-long circular tunnel which now houses the <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">Large Hadron Collider</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Low_Energy_Antiproton_Ring" title="Low Energy Antiproton Ring">Low Energy Antiproton Ring</a> (LEAR), commissioned in 1982, which assembled the first pieces of true <a href="/wiki/Antimatter" title="Antimatter">antimatter</a>, in 1995, consisting of nine atoms of <a href="/wiki/Antihydrogen" title="Antihydrogen">antihydrogen</a>. It was closed in 1996, and superseded by the <a href="/wiki/Antiproton_Decelerator" title="Antiproton Decelerator">Antiproton Decelerator</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_future_accelerators">Possible future accelerators</span></h3>
<p>CERN, in collaboration with groups worldwide, is investigating two main concepts for future accelerators: A linear electron-positron collider with a new acceleration concept to increase the energy (<a href="/wiki/Compact_Linear_Collider" title="Compact Linear Collider">CLIC</a>) and a larger version of the LHC, a project currently named <a href="/wiki/Future_Circular_Collider" title="Future Circular Collider">Future Circular Collider</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sites">Sites</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bldng40cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Bldng40cropped.jpg/220px-Bldng40cropped.jpg" width="220" height="314" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Bldng40cropped.jpg/330px-Bldng40cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Bldng40cropped.jpg/440px-Bldng40cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="2920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bldng40cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of office building 40 at the Meyrin site. Building 40 hosts many offices for scientists from the CMS and ATLAS collaborations.</div></div></div>
<p>The smaller accelerators are on the main <a href="/wiki/Meyrin" title="Meyrin">Meyrin</a> site (also known as the West Area), which was originally built in Switzerland alongside the French border, but has been extended to span the border since 1965. The French side is under Swiss jurisdiction and there is no obvious border within the site, apart from a line of marker stones. There are six entrances to the Meyrin site:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<ul><li><i>A</i>, in Switzerland, for all CERN personnel at specific times.</li>
<li><i>B</i>, in Switzerland, for all CERN personnel at all times. Often referred to as the <i>main entrance</i>.</li>
<li><i>C</i>, in Switzerland, for all CERN personnel at specific times.</li>
<li><i>D</i>, in Switzerland, for goods reception at specific times.</li>
<li><i>E</i>, in France, for French-resident CERN personnel at specific times. Named "Porte Charles de Gaulle" in recognition of his role in the creation of CERN.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Inter-site tunnel</i>, in France, for equipment transfer to and from CERN sites in France by personnel with a specific permit. This is the only permitted route for such transfers. By the CERN treaty, no taxes are payable when such transfers are made. Controlled by customs personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-intersitetunnel_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-intersitetunnel-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CERN-aerial_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/CERN-aerial_1.jpg/220px-CERN-aerial_1.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/CERN-aerial_1.jpg/330px-CERN-aerial_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/CERN-aerial_1.jpg/440px-CERN-aerial_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2432" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CERN-aerial_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>CERN's main site, from <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> looking towards <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a></div></div></div>
<p>The SPS and LEP/LHC tunnels are almost entirely outside the main site, and are mostly buried under French farmland and invisible from the surface. However, they have surface sites at various points around them, either as the location of buildings associated with experiments or other facilities needed to operate the colliders such as cryogenic plants and access shafts. The experiments are located at the same underground level as the tunnels at these sites.
</p><p>Three of these experimental sites are in France, with ATLAS in Switzerland, although some of the ancillary cryogenic and access sites are in Switzerland. The largest of the experimental sites is the <a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%A9vessin" class="mw-redirect" title="Prévessin">Prévessin</a> site, also known as the North Area, which is the target station for non-collider experiments on the SPS accelerator. Other sites are the ones which were used for the <a href="/wiki/UA1_experiment" title="UA1 experiment">UA1</a>, <a href="/wiki/UA2_experiment" title="UA2 experiment">UA2</a> and the LEP experiments (the latter are used by LHC experiments).
</p><p>Outside of the LEP and LHC experiments, most are officially named and numbered after the site where they were located. For example, <a href="/wiki/NA32_experiment" title="NA32 experiment">NA32</a> was an experiment looking at the production of so-called "<a href="/wiki/Charm_quark" title="Charm quark">charmed</a>" particles and located at the <a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%A9vessin" class="mw-redirect" title="Prévessin">Prévessin</a> (North Area) site while <a href="/w/index.php?title=WA22_experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="WA22 experiment (page does not exist)">WA22</a> used the <a href="/wiki/Big_European_Bubble_Chamber" title="Big European Bubble Chamber">Big European Bubble Chamber</a> (BEBC) at the Meyrin (West Area) site to examine neutrino interactions. The <a href="/wiki/UA1_experiment" title="UA1 experiment">UA1</a> and <a href="/wiki/UA2_experiment" title="UA2 experiment">UA2</a> experiments were considered to be in the Underground Area, i.e. situated underground at sites on the SPS accelerator.
</p><p>Most of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_streets_at_CERN" title="List of streets at CERN">roads on the CERN Meyrin and Prévessin sites</a> are named after famous physicists, such as Richard Feynman, Niels Bohr, and Albert Einstein.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Participation_and_funding">Participation and funding</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Member_states_and_budget">Member states and budget</span></h3>
<p>Since its foundation by 12 members in 1954, CERN regularly accepted new members. All new members have remained in the organization continuously since their accession, except Spain and Yugoslavia. Spain first joined CERN in 1961, withdrew in 1969, and rejoined in 1983. Yugoslavia was a founding member of CERN but quit in 1961. Of the 22 members, Israel joined CERN as a full member on 6 January 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-ISR_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISR-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> becoming the first (and currently only) non-European full member.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The budget contributions of member states are computed based on their GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enlargement">Enlargement</span></h3>
<p>Associate Members, Candidates:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="945" data-file-height="630" />&#160;</span>Serbia became a candidate for accession to CERN on 19 December 2011, signed an association agreement on 10 January 2012<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> and became an associate member in the pre-stage to membership on 15 March 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-SRB_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRB-51">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/45px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span>Turkey signed an association agreement on 12 May 2014<sup id="cite_ref-TUR_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TUR-62">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and became an associate member on 6 May 2015.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Flag_of_Pakistan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Pakistan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span>Pakistan signed an association agreement on 19 December 2014<sup id="cite_ref-PAK_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PAK-63">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and became an associate member on 31 July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/23px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/35px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Cyprus.svg/45px-Flag_of_Cyprus.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span>Cyprus signed an association agreement on 5 October 2012 and became an associate Member in the pre-stage to membership on 1 April 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-cyprus-assoc_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cyprus-assoc-52">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Ukraine.svg/45px-Flag_of_Ukraine.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span>Ukraine signed an association agreement on 3 October 2013. The agreement was ratified on 5 October 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-ukraine_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ukraine-57">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/23px-Flag_of_India.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/35px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_India.svg/45px-Flag_of_India.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1350" data-file-height="900" />&#160;</span>India signed an association agreement on 21 November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The agreement was ratified on 16 January 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-india_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-india-58">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Slovenia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Slovenia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Slovenia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Slovenia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Flag_of_Slovenia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Slovenia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span>Slovenia was approved for admission as an Associate Member state in the pre-stage to membership on 16 December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-slovenia-assoc_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slovenia-assoc-53">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The agreement was ratified on 4 July 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-slovenia-assoc-ratify_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slovenia-assoc-ratify-54">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Flag_of_Lithuania.svg/23px-Flag_of_Lithuania.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Flag_of_Lithuania.svg/35px-Flag_of_Lithuania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Flag_of_Lithuania.svg/46px-Flag_of_Lithuania.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="300" />&#160;</span>Lithuania was approved for admission as an Associate Member state on 16 June 2017. The association agreement was signed on 27 June 2017 and ratified on 8 January 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-lithuania-assoc-lrp_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lithuania-assoc-lrp-67">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lithuania-assoc-cern_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lithuania-assoc-cern-59">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span></h3>
<p>Three countries have observer status:<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span>Japan – since 1995</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span>Russia – since 1993</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" />&#160;</span>United States – since 1997</li></ul></div>
<p>Also observers are the following international organizations:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Flag_of_UNESCO.svg/23px-Flag_of_UNESCO.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Flag_of_UNESCO.svg/35px-Flag_of_UNESCO.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Flag_of_UNESCO.svg/45px-Flag_of_UNESCO.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> – since 1954</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe"><img alt="Europe" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/45px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="540" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> – since 1985</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joint_Institute_for_Nuclear_Research" title="Joint Institute for Nuclear Research">JINR</a> - since 2014</li></ul>

<p>International research institutions, such as CERN, can aid in science diplomacy.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Associated_institutions">Associated institutions</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ESO_and_CERN_sign_cooperation_agreement.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/ESO_and_CERN_sign_cooperation_agreement.jpg/150px-ESO_and_CERN_sign_cooperation_agreement.jpg" width="150" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/ESO_and_CERN_sign_cooperation_agreement.jpg/225px-ESO_and_CERN_sign_cooperation_agreement.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/ESO_and_CERN_sign_cooperation_agreement.jpg/300px-ESO_and_CERN_sign_cooperation_agreement.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="853" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ESO_and_CERN_sign_cooperation_agreement.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/ESO" class="mw-redirect" title="ESO">ESO</a> and CERN have a cooperation agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-ESO-201310_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESO-201310-75">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=CERN&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small><i>(October 2013)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/European_Southern_Observatory" title="European Southern Observatory">European Southern Observatory</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Swiss_National_Supercomputing_Centre" title="Swiss National Supercomputing Centre">Swiss National Supercomputing Centre</a></li></ul>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_access_publishing">Open access publishing</span></h2>
<p>CERN has initiated an <a href="/wiki/Open_access" title="Open access">open access</a> publishing project to convert scientific articles in high energy physics into <a href="/wiki/Gold_open_access" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold open access">gold open access</a> by redirecting subscription fees. In the first phase from 2014-2016 3,000 libraries, consortia, research organisations, publishers and funding agencies in various countries participated.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> All publications by CERN authors are published with gold open access.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_exhibits">Public exhibits</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CERN_Globe_of_Science_and_Innovation.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/CERN_Globe_of_Science_and_Innovation.jpg/220px-CERN_Globe_of_Science_and_Innovation.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/CERN_Globe_of_Science_and_Innovation.jpg/330px-CERN_Globe_of_Science_and_Innovation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/CERN_Globe_of_Science_and_Innovation.jpg/440px-CERN_Globe_of_Science_and_Innovation.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CERN_Globe_of_Science_and_Innovation.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Globe_of_Science_and_Innovation" title="The Globe of Science and Innovation">The Globe of Science and Innovation</a> at CERN</div></div></div>
<p>Facilities at CERN open to the public include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/The_Globe_of_Science_and_Innovation" title="The Globe of Science and Innovation">The Globe of Science and Innovation</a>, which opened in late 2005 and is used four times a week for special exhibits.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Microcosm_(CERN)" title="Microcosm (CERN)">Microcosm museum</a> on <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">particle physics</a> and CERN history.</li></ul>
<p>CERN also provides daily tours to certain facilities such as the Synchro-cyclotron (CERNs first particle accelerator) and the superconducting magnet workshop.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CERN_Tram,_line_number_18.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/CERN_Tram%2C_line_number_18.jpg/220px-CERN_Tram%2C_line_number_18.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/CERN_Tram%2C_line_number_18.jpg/330px-CERN_Tram%2C_line_number_18.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/CERN_Tram%2C_line_number_18.jpg/440px-CERN_Tram%2C_line_number_18.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1141" data-file-height="760" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CERN_Tram,_line_number_18.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Line 18 goes to CERN</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shiva%27s_statue_at_CERN_engaging_in_the_Nataraja_dance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Shiva%27s_statue_at_CERN_engaging_in_the_Nataraja_dance.jpg/170px-Shiva%27s_statue_at_CERN_engaging_in_the_Nataraja_dance.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Shiva%27s_statue_at_CERN_engaging_in_the_Nataraja_dance.jpg/255px-Shiva%27s_statue_at_CERN_engaging_in_the_Nataraja_dance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Shiva%27s_statue_at_CERN_engaging_in_the_Nataraja_dance.jpg/340px-Shiva%27s_statue_at_CERN_engaging_in_the_Nataraja_dance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1365" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shiva%27s_statue_at_CERN_engaging_in_the_Nataraja_dance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The statue of <a href="/wiki/Shiva" title="Shiva">Shiva</a> engaging in the <a href="/wiki/Nataraja" title="Nataraja">Nataraja</a> dance presented by the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Atomic_Energy" title="Department of Atomic Energy">Department of Atomic Energy</a> of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>.</div></div></div>
<ul><li>The band <a href="/wiki/Les_Horribles_Cernettes" title="Les Horribles Cernettes">Les Horribles Cernettes</a> was founded by women from CERN. The name was chosen so to have the same initials as the LHC.<sup id="cite_ref-CernettesNYT_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CernettesNYT-78">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CernettesWired_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CernettesWired-79">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>CERN's Large Hadron Collider is the subject of a (scientifically accurate) <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">rap</a> video starring <a href="/wiki/Katherine_McAlpine" title="Katherine McAlpine">Katherine McAlpine</a> with some of the facility's staff.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Particle_Fever" title="Particle Fever">Particle Fever</a></i>, a 2013 documentary, explores CERN throughout the inside and depicts the events surrounding the 2012 discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Higgs_Boson" class="mw-redirect" title="Higgs Boson">Higgs Boson</a></li>
<li>CERN is depicted in an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/South_Park" title="South Park">South Park</a></i> (Season 13, Episode 6) called "Pinewood Derby". Randy Marsh, the father of one of the main characters, breaks into the "Hadron Particle Super Collider in Switzerland" and steals a "superconducting bending magnet created for use in tests with particle acceleration" to use in his son Stan's Pinewood Derby racer. Randy breaks into CERN dressed in disguise as Princess Leia from the <i>Star Wars</i> saga. The break-in is captured on surveillance tape which is then broadcast on the news.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Titor" title="John Titor">John Titor</a>, a self-proclaimed <a href="/wiki/Time_travel" title="Time travel">time traveler</a>, alleged that CERN would invent time travel in 2001.</li>
<li>CERN is depicted in the <a href="/wiki/Visual_novel" title="Visual novel">visual novel</a>/<a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Steins;Gate" title="Steins;Gate">Steins;Gate</a></i> as SERN, a shadowy organization that has been researching time travel in order to restructure and control the world.</li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Dan_Brown" title="Dan Brown">Dan Brown</a>'s mystery-thriller novel <i><a href="/wiki/Angels_%26_Demons" title="Angels &amp; Demons">Angels &amp; Demons</a></i> and film <a href="/wiki/Angels_%26_Demons_(film)" title="Angels &amp; Demons (film)">of the same name</a>, a canister of antimatter is stolen from CERN.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In the popular children's series <i><a href="/wiki/The_39_Clues" title="The 39 Clues">The 39 Clues</a></i>, CERN is said to be an Ekaterina stronghold hiding the clue hydrogen.</li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Robert_J._Sawyer" title="Robert J. Sawyer">Robert J. Sawyer</a>'s science fiction novel <i><a href="/wiki/Flashforward_(novel)" title="Flashforward (novel)">Flashforward</a></i>, at CERN, the Large Hadron Collider accelerator is performing a run to search for the Higgs boson when the entire human race sees themselves twenty-one years and six months in the future.</li>
<li>In season 3 episode 15 of the TV sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/The_Big_Bang_Theory" title="The Big Bang Theory">The Big Bang Theory</a></i> titled "The Large Hadron Collision", <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Hofstadter" title="Leonard Hofstadter">Leonard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raj_Koothrappali" title="Raj Koothrappali">Raj</a> travel to CERN to attend a conference and see the LHC.</li>
<li>The 2012 student film <i><a href="/wiki/Decay_(2012_film)" title="Decay (2012 film)">Decay</a></i>, which centers on the idea of the Large Hadron Collider transforming people into zombies, was filmed on location in CERN's maintenance tunnels.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Compact Muon Solenoid at CERN was used as the basis for the <a href="/wiki/Megadeth" title="Megadeth">Megadeth</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Super_Collider_(album)" title="Super Collider (album)"><i>Super Collider</i></a> album cover.</li>
<li>In <i>Super Lovers</i>, Haruko (Ren's mother) worked at CERN, and Ren was taught by CERN professors</li>
<li>CERN forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Back_story" class="mw-redirect" title="Back story">back story</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Massively_multiplayer_online_role_playing_game" class="mw-redirect" title="Massively multiplayer online role playing game">massively multiplayer</a> <a href="/wiki/Augmented_reality" title="Augmented reality">augmented reality</a> game <i><a href="/wiki/Ingress_(game)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ingress (game)">Ingress</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In season 10 episode 6 of the BBC TV show <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">Doctor Who</a></i> titled <a href="/wiki/Extremis_(Doctor_Who)" title="Extremis (Doctor Who)">"Extremis"</a>, CERN and its physicists are involved in a mysterious plot involving a book that causes everyone who reads it to kill themselves.</li></ul>
